Page 12

Chunqiu (Spring and Autumn)

Reform of Private Schools

— Zhanlu

The term "reform of private schools" appears from time to time in educational news. Upon seeing this term, I cannot help but recall the work of private school reform twenty-nine years ago.

At that time, my colleagues from the Jiangsu Provincial Higher School organized a night school for a Private School Reform Association in Suzhou, recruiting general private school teachers to teach them simple normal school methods. I was in charge of grammar, and when I lectured on the usage of nouns, pronouns, verbs, adjectives, etc., it aroused the interest of many private school teachers who were twice my age, simply because they had never heard of it before.

Later, the school gradually developed, and the call for private school reform gradually faded. Now, nearly thirty years later, the slogan of private school reform is suddenly being shouted again, which makes me feel bewildered. If private schools needed reform twenty-nine years ago, and they still need reform twenty-nine years later, when will they ever be reformed? The equipment of private schools is very simple, yet they have been reformed for nearly thirty years without improvement. What else can be said?

Recently, the magistrate of Sanshui County, Guangdong Province, has ordered the sealing and dissolution of all private schools. For those who disobey, the county government has ordered the Public Security Bureau, saying: "They dare to disobey orders while the ink is not yet dry, which is an extreme violation of the law. The director of the bureau is ordered to immediately expel the teachers from the county. If they continue to resist, they will be arrested and brought to the government for punishment." This decisive magistrate of Sanshui County treats teachers as bandits. He believes that private schools are all bad and is fundamentally eliminating them, which is certainly a very straightforward approach. However, I fear that the teachers will ask in return: "If private schools are bad, are all schools really good?" I believe that a compromise solution is needed: the reform of private schools and the reform of schools should proceed simultaneously.

Dream Talk

— Hualing

Those semi-traitorous, soon-to-be-enslaved people, craning their necks and respectfully waiting for the Imperial Army to raise their hands and grant them the honor of tasting a Japanese sword, if they want to be happy, the best way is still to rest their heads on a high, three-foot-three-inch pillow and pursue a dream of paradise.

A bellyful of righteous indignation, wanting to take the stage to express myself, or announce it with my pen, but I cannot bear to sacrifice the rice bowl that I have shared with the enemy for decades, so I am timid and shrinking, and finally just shrink my head. In a dream, you can speak frankly without being blamed.

A bellyful of articles about governing the country and pacifying the world, having fished out all the big and small fish in Qinhuai and Xuanwu, but alas, no King Wen is even glancing at me. In a dream, I can overthrow you, and I can come.

Those who do not have a good appetite do not expect these, but seeing how Brother Zhang has hoarded silver and gold, dancing with beautiful women, and playing golf with foreigners, how can they not be envious? In a dream, I want more than anyone, to be even happier than him.

Looking for food, spitting out all my anger. Looking at the boss, not even the big boss's face is enough, the head clerk, the second clerk, will also put on a pretentious air. Even if I spit out all my anger, I have to swallow the broken teeth down into my stomach. In a dream, I can overthrow those who should be overthrown, and expel those who should be expelled, to vent my anger.

After twelve hours of sweating, the reward I get is not enough to fill the stomachs of my family of eight. On the first and fifteenth of the month, when I want to eat meat, I buy three hundred cash worth of pork neck, but I have already borrowed two hundred cash with high interest. In a dream, I can feast without paying.

All year round, the medicine pot never leaves my side, and I am as thin as a twig. The efficacy of the medicine is like plain water, I am just in a hurry, and I have no hope of getting out of bed. In a dream, I can regain my health, go to Hangzhou, visit Longhua, and do whatever I want.

The most perfect people have no dreams, and fools talk about dreams. But even our great sage and teacher Confucius still dreamed of the Duke of Zhou. It can be seen that dreaming is not something that cannot be brought into the hall of elegance.

In this era, nine out of ten people are running into walls everywhere. Being a monk, jumping into the Huangpu River, not knowing how to have fun in a dream, are all fools. To live drunk and die dreaming, to see life as a dream, is to be perfect.

On Seeing a Rubbing of a Bronze Bell Presented by a Buddhist Association as a Memorial to the Japanese Earthquake, I Composed a Poem; at That Time, There Was Another Earthquake in Hokkaido, Japan, and the Battle of Rehe Was in Full Swing

— Jiamenglū

After the bell rings, the sound of cannons comes, and the haze over the mainland does not dissipate. Not living under the same sky nor treading the same earth, who remembers this lung and liver being torn apart?

Wiping away the red kerchief to mourn the nation, the people are still in dire straits. The Pu Lao roars across the sea, can its voice be heard on the battlefield?

Skill in warfare has always been a top punishment, how can repentance reach the underworld? The hearts of the people are dead, and Heaven is tired of it, no wonder the rocks stir up the anger of thunder.

God is silent, and a hundred ghosts are snarling, (borrowed line) myriad grievances are among the living. The blood flowers fly, and the heavenly flowers fall, the pestle of the clear bell illuminates the bright moon.

If the poetry circles in the country would like to offer a harmony (regardless of style), I respectfully offer Yi Shifu's Qin Zhi Lou poems in return, a total of eight volumes of mountain travel poems, twelve volumes of chronological poems, and four volumes of poems from the Renzi and Jiayin years. The amount of return will be determined on a case-by-case basis. The entire collection is stored in one box and will be given away until it is empty. Correspondence address: Shanghai News Fukangli 17.

Full-Length Novel

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Five

Brewing Tea to Pass the Long Night, Grieving at the Year's End

Addressing the Violent Day of Resistance, Shouting Loudly

Yang Guizhi was about to argue with the shop assistant at the pawnshop over the one dollar difference in the price of the clothing when someone called out from behind. Turning around, she saw Zhao Ziqiang running after her. Guizhi blushed and said, "Company Commander Zhao, you've come here too." Zhao Ziqiang laughed, "I heard my orderly say that the 'old girl' took the cotton clothing out the front gate, so I asked your old mother what that was about. Your old mother said that they were still short three dollars for the New Year and had taken the clothing to pawn for money. I thought, why make such a fuss over such a small matter and pawn your cotton clothes in this cold weather? We'll get paid soon for the New Year; I can cover it for you. Let's go back." As he spoke, he took the roll of clothing down from the counter, tucked it under his arm, and led the way. At this point, the "old girl" couldn't help but follow him, and she resented the pawnshop assistant for being so unfeeling. She turned back and glared fiercely at the assistant behind the counter, then followed Zhao Ziqiang out onto the street. This Company Commander Zhao was different from Gan Erye. He was very reserved, always walking ahead of Guizhi without turning his head, let alone talking. The two hurried along, and soon arrived at the house. Jiang was already at the front gate, taking the clothing with both hands and bowing repeatedly to Zhao Ziqiang, saying, "Thank you, thank you, how could we ask you to help us with such a big favor? After the New Year, when I have some money, I'll definitely repay you in full." After speaking to Zhao Ziqiang she said to Guizhi: "You don't know, Company Commander Zhao is such a good person. He heard that our family was being pressed by creditors and lent them five dollars for the New Year, so they have money to spend after paying off their debts. How can we feel good about letting Company Commander Zhao help us with such a big favor for no reason?" Zhao Ziqiang smiled and waved his hands twice, saying, "Don't say it, don't say it, it's embarrassing to talk about it." Without waiting for Jiang to say anything more, he walked away. Guizhi walked into the house, frowning and complaining to her mother, "You're acting recklessly. How can we accept money from someone for no reason?" Jiang said, "I said so too. But he specifically came to ask me, so I couldn't help but tell the truth." (48)

Random Notes on a Poor Spring

— Huo Xueming

Since the beginning of spring, the weather has been quite cool and cold. Although the plum blossoms have already bloomed and are now fading, the peach blossoms are definitely blooming later than in previous years.

The northeast wind has been blowing constantly. Waking up in the morning, the warm sunshine from the morning sun warms the pillow, and I smile inwardly, thinking, "On such a clear and bright spring morning, wouldn't you want to go to Nanping to listen to the bells of the ancient temple?"

However, from the distant forest, I hear the diligent cries of the quails. In our village, there's a folk song that says: "Quail, much wind and much rain." My brows furrow again. It seems that the cries of these birds can predict wind and rain. Often, farmers carry umbrellas in the sunlight to the market, only to return to the village in the rain.

The sunny mornings are like the weather in May, and you can wear a single shirt. But then a strong wind blows, black clouds swell up and spread like ink, and cold rain pours down torrentially. Small ditches can be used for swimming ducklings, and the shadows of sails can float up to the second floor. At that time, if you don't wear a thick camel wool robe, your temples will soon start to burn. There's a saying in the village: "When going out, beware of the third and ninth months." That refers to the lunar calendar, but it's said to be very accurate.

On this day two years ago, after viewing the plum blossoms at Damingtang in Chaoshan (now damaged by thieves), I returned to Tangqi by boat. The weather was still clear, sunny, and warm. But in the afternoon, as I went with the monk Shipiao to the Hupao Temple, the wind and clouds suddenly changed color. Rain, mixed with snow, fell in a flurry, followed by hailstones. I was wearing a woolen hat, so it wasn't so bad, but Shipiao's bald head was hit by egg-sized hailstones, breaking the skin and splattering out bright red blood. We had to take temporary shelter under a small tree for a while. By the time the hail stopped and we continued on, our clothes were completely soaked. Shipiao still has scars on his head to this day, so he's also known as "Sick Gourd," and is currently reciting scriptures at the Jingci Temple in Hangzhou. As for me, I caught a bout of malarial fever upon returning to Shanghai.

Because of this lesson, in this strange year, I'm afraid of being tricked by the unpredictable weather, and I'm not carrying many heavy items when I travel. That's why I'm still wandering around in Shanghai, a city that devours souls, from early morning to late at night.

After Visiting the Sincere Company's Exhibition of National Products in Hong Kong

— Wenpu

I came from Southeast Asia, passing through Hong Kong. Having heard that the Sincere Company was holding an exhibition of national products, I visited it once. Seeing that this kind of exhibition is of great importance to people's livelihoods, and is especially urgent for our country at the present time, I have written this account to serve as a model for large department stores in various cities, as a means of learning from each other.

The exhibition hall was set up on the company's rooftop, with beautiful arrangements and orderly organization. Silk fabrics, cotton fabrics, and other products were categorized and displayed in order. Participating manufacturers came from Hong Kong, Guangzhou, and Shanghai, totaling dozens of companies. Visitors came to see the exhibition enthusiastically. Famous figures such as Cai Tingkai, Tan Qixiu, Liu Jiwen, Zhang Yan, and Zou Minchu, among others, all visited the exhibition one after another. Various groups and organizations also came in teams, which was enough to demonstrate the public's mentality of loving and using national products. It was truly an encouraging act amidst the national crisis. I have lived in Southeast Asia for several decades. There, the overseas Chinese depend on foreigners for their clothing, food, and housing. Although they have the desire to love and use national products, there are actually no exquisite national products to buy. The money spent on foreign goods each year amounts to no less than ten million. Now that national products have made such progress and are so excellent, if overseas Chinese can be made aware of this, they will surely be happy to adopt and compete to buy them. I sincerely hope that the Sincere Company's authorities will gradually expand the national product exhibition to promote national products, arouse the public to uniformly use national products, and make the public generally recognize the advantages of national products. The national economy and people's livelihoods will truly benefit from this.

Small Recipes

Spring Bamboo Shoots

— Rongyu

Swallows are chattering and murmuring on the beams; tender shoots are emerging from the soil in the bamboo groves. This is truly the harmonious season of spring, and also the time when swallow bamboo shoots are on the market.

Jiangsu and Zhejiang have a lot of bamboo planting, no matter in the mountains or on the plains, thousands of jade green poles and tens of thousands of emerald hairpin-like leaves are everywhere. However, the shoots that grow in the mountain bamboo forests are large and hairy, commonly called "hairy shoots," and are suitable for roasting or drying. Those dug in the bamboo gardens in the countryside have different names depending on the season. In February and March, they are called "swallow shoots" because the swallows are just returning from the south at this time. Later, they are called "chicken shoots" because it is truly the time when chicks hatch. The latest kind is called "late sprout shoots," which are available in mid-May.

Invite three or five good friends, buy a jar of country wine, and call the village children to dig fresh bamboo shoots in the bamboo garden, then immediately ask the family to cook them. The bamboo flavor is tender and sweet; the bamboo soup is fresh and clean. Such flavors are probably hard to come by in Shanghai.

As soon as the thunder roars, the bamboo shoots grow rapidly. If the weather is sunny and cold, they grow very slowly. Not only do people like to chew on them, but wild boars and other animals secretly run into the bamboo garden on windy and moonless nights to eat them raw and whole.

The bamboo of Ningdong is the hairy bamboo mentioned above. Every year, a "shoot king" emerges, which is extraordinarily large. There are two shoots beside it that are slightly shorter, called "shoot generals." The outer skin of the shoot tip has a brocade band that is more than a foot long, like the pheasant feathers that ancient people inserted in their hats. People don't dare to dig and eat them. If they accidentally remove them, the family will suffer a strange disaster. This is recorded in ancient books. Whether or not this is true remains to be asked of the people of this place.

Baby Coconut

— Zhang Yian

Recently, I heard that coconut shell ash (charcoal?) can be used for military defense against poisonous gas, so I thought of everything about coconuts.

Coconuts originally come from the islands of Southeast Asia, but quite a few are imported to Guangdong every year. Therefore, coconuts have become a very popular food in Guangdong, and there is no one in Guangdong who does not know coconuts.

If you go to Guangdong, the easiest place to find coconuts is on the stands selling "salty, sour, and sweet" snacks. Every "salty, sour, and sweet" stand or stall has coconuts, cut into triangular pieces or long strips, as white as mutton fat jade, soaked in clear water. And, sellers of coconuts on "salty, sour, and sweet" stands always sell them together with pickled ginger slices. People who eat them also like to eat both together.

The term "salty, sour, and sweet" stand can be understood by its name. The stand sells pickled, sour, salty, and sweet fruits and vegetables, such as pickled cucumbers, vinegar-soaked mustard tubers, sour and spicy vegetables, pickled radishes, pickled chili peppers, sweet papaya slices, and salty sand pears. Salty items include jellyfish and loach. The stand has a small stove and pot, ready to cook jellyfish and loach. This kind of stand can also be seen in the Hongkou area of Shanghai.

When I was young, both pickled ginger and coconuts sold for two small coins a slice. Now, coconuts sell for two or three copper coins.

Coconuts also have a place in the New Year's candy box. They are cooked with sugar and dried. One type is cut into flat strips, called sugar coconut shreds, and the other is cut into triangular blocks, called sugar coconut cubes. Because it has a lot of residue and little juice, I never liked to eat it much.

Also, half a coconut is used in engagement gifts, shaped like a ladle, with dragon, phoenix, and double happiness patterns painted on it in gold.

Now, pastry shops have a type of pastry called coconut tart (tart is a transliteration of "tart"), which is topped with very fine coconut shreds mixed with sugar juice.

Coconut juice, extracted by grinding the coconut, must be added to curry chicken to make it taste good. Outsiders who make curry chicken don't understand this point and will never make good curry chicken.

After buying a whole coconut to take home, first remove the coconut husk, and then use a nail or similar object to make a hole in the coconut shell, letting the coconut juice, a white liquid like milk, flow out. This juice is not very useful except as a drink, and it tastes slightly sweet. Then, use a saw to cut the coconut shell in half. After the coconut meat is dug out for eating, the two halves of the coconut shell are used as water ladles. Guangdong soldiers often carry such a coconut ladle with them. Sometimes, when the coconut ladle breaks, the pieces become materials for our handicrafts.

Free Talk Hengzhi

"Using Barbarians to Control Barbarians"

— He Jiagan

I still remember that when many people in China were complaining to the League of Nations last year, Japanese newspapers often ridiculed them, saying that this was the old trick of "using barbarians to control barbarians" inherited from Chinese ancestors. At first glance, it seemed somewhat similar, but in reality, it was not. At that time, many people in China indeed regarded the League of Nations as the "just and upright official," and there was not even a trace of the word "barbarian" in their minds.

On the contrary, the "just and upright officials" often used the method of "using Chinese to control Chinese."

For example, the "criminals" who they deeply hated for being anti-imperialist were not made villains by them, but were freely and easily handed over to the Chinese, telling you to kill them yourself. The "Communist bandits" in the hinterland, whom they hated, were not explicitly commented upon by them, but they sold airplanes and bombs to the Chinese, telling you to bomb them yourself. The lower-class Chinese were dealt with by Huangdi's descendants who were police and compradors, and the intellectual class were dealt with by "upper-class Chinese" scholars and doctors.

The "Big Sword Team," which we had boasted about for many days, seemed impossible to subdue, but on April 15th, the "XX Newspaper" had a headline printed in the largest font: "I Slew 200 Enemies." At first glance, it was meant to make people feel victorious, but let's take a look at the content of the article:

" (This newspaper's Beiping dispatch today) Last night on the right wing of Xifengkou, fierce battles continued in various places east of Luanyangcheng. The enemy appeared with a Big Sword Team of a thousand men, newly arrived, confronting our Big Sword Team. Their swords were especially long, making them clumsy to use. Our army swung their swords and slashed, and the enemy was unable to block and parry. Arms and swords were cut off and lay scattered all over the ground. Our army's casualties also reached over two hundred."

So, this was actually "the enemy slew 200 of our soldiers." Chinese writing is truly becoming more and more difficult, like the "national gait." But that is not what I want to point out.

What I want to point out is that the "Big Sword Team" is a specialty that the Chinese have boasted about for a long time. Although the Japanese have swordsmanship, they are not accustomed to using the big sword. Now that they have "appeared," there is no need to hesitate to decide that they are Manchurian troops. Since the end of the Ming Dynasty, many people from Zhili and Shandong have migrated to Manchuria every year. After several generations, they have become natives, so even though they are Manchurian troops, the majority are actually Chinese, and there is no doubt about it. Now that they have each used their specialties, the big sword, they are killing each other in Luandong, with one side "arms and swords, scattered all over the ground" and the other side "casualties also reached over two hundred," enacting a very prominent scene of "using Chinese to control Chinese."

As for China's so-called methods, from my perspective, we should say that they exist, but they are definitely not "using barbarians to control barbarians," but rather wanting to "use barbarians to control the Chinese." However, how could the "barbarians" be so foolish? They first give you a set of "using Chinese to control Chinese" to watch.

This example is often seen in Chinese history. Later historians wrote eulogies for the new dynasty, calling the actions of these people "forerunners for the king"! Recent war reports are extremely astonishing. The same day, the same newspaper reported the loss of Lengkou, saying: "After the tenth day, the battle on the Lengkou front was extremely fierce. The Chinese army stubbornly resisted, hence a great battle of unprecedented intensity continued." But the Miyazaki unit, with more than ten soldiers, formed a human ladder, falling one after another, "finally crossed the Great Wall, therefore the Miyazaki unit sacrificed as many as twenty-three men." Crossing a dangerous pass, and the Japanese army only lost twenty-three men, but it is said to be "as many," and also called "a great battle of unprecedented intensity," which is a bit puzzling. Therefore, the battle of the Big Sword Team may not be as I guessed. But since it has been written, let it be left for one explanation.

Internal and External Supplements

— Zhou Muzhai

Mr. He Jiagan, in his "Internal and External" essay, elucidated the reasons for differentiating between internal and external and the different methods of governing the mind, which was extremely thorough and can be read as a "record of sayings" of the Song Confucians. However, I feel that there are still omissions, so I venture to supplement some opinions, despite my humble abilities. Fortunately, we are now in the flourishing age of promoting the learning of Wang Yangming, and blessed by his virtue, we lowly people seem to have a duty to make some timely embellishments.

Distinguishing between internal and external is, according to the Song Confucians, only the initial step. When discussing it with true subtlety, there is also the so-called way of unifying internal and external, having no external without internal, unifying the external within the internal. Therefore, this internal is the "internal without external." At the same time, even within the mind, there is the distinction between "expressed" and "unexpressed." The intention is none other than to say: Don't care about the outside, but if you can take care of the inside, then you will have unlimited applications. Moreover, "expressed" means having a form or trace, while "unexpressed" is the whole, indescribable and unrevealable. As the ancients said, "The moral mind is subtle, the human mind is perilous." This is what it means.

When the Song dynasty suffered the disasters of the Liao and Jin dynasties, it is said that "Song learning" was the medicine to save the hearts of the people at that time. Now that China is in the same situation as the Song dynasty, but the Liao and Jin dynasties have been replaced by Japan, the same social situation produces the same state of consciousness and emotion. No wonder "Song learning" is reviving. The object of external trouble has changed, but what remains unchanged is China.

Some people doubt that the rise of "Song learning" ultimately could not save the Song dynasty from its demise. In fact, "Song learning" was a miscarriage when the Song dynasty was on the verge of demise. What is suppressed in one area must be stretched out in another. Since one has met a wall externally, one can only turn inward to seek.

In the end, the Liao and Jin dynasties did not destroy the Song dynasty. It was the Yuan who destroyed the Song!

Rainy Day

— Sha Tuo

Waking up, I saw water droplets dripping on the window, rain drifting outside the window, and I thought to myself, "Oh no! I have to endure another rainy day!"

In Shanghai, the rain gives me a really bad impression. Shanghai is originally a place of intense business, and most people are bustling and hurrying, racing in the field of profit every day, and they also have no leisurely mood to care about whether the weather is good or bad. But sunny days are always better than rainy days, and everyone should agree with this. Whether it's a poet in a small attic room bored to death, or an office worker in a writing room busy beyond description, on a sunny day there is always a chance to face the blue sky and the white clouds floating piece by piece, making sweet spring dreams. But rainy days are not like that. They give you only a feeling of stuffiness, turbidity, dampness, and helplessness. Everyone sighs with a bitter face at the gray and black sky. Whether indoors or on the street, it always makes you uncomfortable.

But this is only in Shanghai. In some places, rain is not particularly annoying. Like in the mountains of my hometown, rainy days are interesting beyond compare.

When I was a child, on such rainy days, I liked to stand on the second floor of the side building and gaze out. Below the building was a stream, its water somewhat turbid, flowing swiftly, spraying white foam on the sandy rocks. Opposite was the mountain, with clouds often spitting out from between the peaks, each with a different color and shape. The distant mountains were shrouded in mist. The rain hung before my eyes like a gauze curtain. Cobwebs were stretched on the old corners of the house, and many sparkling water droplets were entangled on the webs. Ducks in the pond were bending their necks, preening their feathers, and quacking loudly and happily. My sisters were weaving ribbons or embroidering downstairs, and my mother was spinning yarn in the outer room. The sound of the spinning wheel corresponded to the sound of the rain in front of the steps. My body was soaked by the rain. One moment I was nibbling on New Year cake, and the next I was clinging to my mother, arguing for this and wanting that. My mother always smiled gently. The same rainy day, but how happy, how memorable!

Three years ago, while living in Tokyo, it was also such a rainy day. I sat on the tatami mat, leaning against the brazier. The small four-and-a-half-mat room was full of exotic atmosphere. I quietly listened to the sound of the rain hitting the lead roof, and unconsciously felt the homesickness and travel sorrows common to wanderers. Just as I was about to feel extremely desolate, a burst of singing suddenly came from over there, melodious and beautiful. This was the most popular folk song in the island country, "The Girl of the Red Roof!" The same rainy day, but how beautiful, how poetic!

Now everything is over, everything has become an elusive trace of the past. I can no longer see the beautiful scenery of my hometown, nor can I hear the love songs of a foreign land. I am only lurking in a dark corner of this ugly metropolis, listening to the continuous spring rain, relentlessly, stubbornly dripping, dripping, making people feel depressed, irritable, and endlessly sentimental!

Hometown Miscellany

— Mu Shiying

3. My Home and Miss Ling's Home

Around ten o'clock, we took the train to Cixi. This strange city of fish and salt was thrown behind us. The train carriages there were much smaller and slower than the Shanghai-Hangzhou and Shanghai-Ningbo lines, but we only sat for fifteen minutes before we arrived at Cixi. I almost laughed again; I felt like I was playing the protagonist in a slapstick movie, thinking that we would have to sit for at least two or three hours, but who knew that we would arrive after smoking a cigarette. Leaving the train station, we stepped out of the twentieth century. That long, narrow stone road stretched out in front of us, and a sedan chair floated above it, moving towards the mountain shadows, as if walking into a medieval ancient dream.

The station was still seven miles away from our house, the courtyard that had been locked up for eight years. The villagers were probably waiting for us at the gate to have lunch. The calla lilies must have bloomed, because the fields were already full of yellow rapeseed flowers, and the cuckoo's call was rippling in the spring breeze.

We walked quickly, and slowly, the white courtyard wall of our house stood out among the rapeseed flowers, and the green moss in the pond in front of the gate faintly reflected the bronze-colored sunlight.

"We're home! This time, we're really home!"

The three of us brothers broke into a run, no longer caring about our old uncle who was watching the scenery behind us. As we ran, the white courtyard wall became clearer, and the people sitting on the bridge over the small river in front of the gate could be seen clearly! Our home was there. Our home was there!

Running to the gate, suddenly several dogs rushed out barking at us. The people inside the house were scolding the dogs while looking at us, as if they didn't recognize us. After a while, they smiled and pointed at us, saying, "This is so-and-so's son, that is so-and-so's son." We didn't care about anything and rushed straight in. When we got to the house, our aunts and uncles had already arrived three days before us and were preparing tea and water to wait for us. I didn't even wash my face before running to the flower hall. The orange tree was blooming even more luxuriantly than before, and a large bodhi tree in the courtyard had grown taller than the house. The calla lilies wrapped around my feet. They still recognized me, because they smiled happily. I stood there silently, and my childhood memories came back to me one by one. I had listened to my grandmother telling stories under this bodhi tree, I had secretly stolen sugarcane to eat in that small room over there, and I had ridden that big dog called A'huang in this courtyard, thinking that I was riding through the streets after being selected as the third scholar. Now I am a twenty-two-year-old young man, but my grandmother is dead, A'huang is also dead, and the pillars of the house seem to be older than before. Memories will come back, but reality will not come back again.

In the afternoon, we went to an aunt's house. There were seven of us in total, walking and laughing in the fields. My aunt's family was a large family in Ningbo, which was also Miss Ling's home. I had been there once when I was a child, but I didn't have much of an impression. This time, I was able to run there again, and I didn't think the crowding on the boat that night was anything. The house was really scary big. From entering the gate to my aunt's house, we walked through that dark corridor for half a day. I seemed to recognize all those houses, because the girl grew up here. As I went, I looked around; I wanted to know which room was where Miss Ling grew up. There was no one in those courtyards and houses, desolate, locked with the coolness of late autumn. Turning a corner, we walked into my aunt's house, and she had already seen us and came out smiling with her granddaughter in her arms. I hadn't seen her for almost three years. After Miss Ling died, I hadn't been to her house.

They talked for a while and then started playing cards. I sat alone by the window, holding her granddaughter and playing. She was a very cute girl. She was very happy to be with me, but she was also shy, with that kind of true and false appearance, so much like Miss Ling! The child was also four years old. Yes, Miss Ling had been dead for three years. She was now lying quietly under the marble in the International Cemetery. My aunt saw that I was having fun playing with her and said with a smile, "You really like her." I really like her, because she also has the lilac's flavor of remembrance!

I don't know what time it started, but it was drizzling outside the window, fine and light. In the dim sound of rain, the sky darkened. Facing this dim lamplight, I felt every raindrop dripping on my heart, and every drop of rain evoked old memories and old melancholy in my heart.

I was at Miss Ling's house; where was Miss Ling? Where was Miss Ling? Lilac's flavor of remembrance!

I stiffened my face and started playing with dolls with the child again.

Long Novel

The Crossroads of Era and Love

— Zhang Ziping

Although he asked her that, he felt a wave of chills running through his body. It was late at night, and the weather was indeed getting colder. His teeth chattered and clacked together. He could hardly form words.

"Mr. Lin, would you go down and take a look?"

America Abandons the Gold Standard

The Gold Market Experiences a Major Plunge

America Reinstates the Gold Ban, Silver Prices Rise Astonishingly

Negative News Abounds, Buyers Rarely Seen

Lowest at 966 Yuan, a Sharp Drop of 84.7 Yuan

The gold market has been full of twists and turns. Yesterday, the market experienced another major plunge. In the early morning, due to foreign telegrams indicating that London's near and distant futures both increased by 4.375, and Bank of America rose by 3.5 points, the British-American and American-British exchange rates rose by as much as 13.5 and 19.5 points respectively. The spot silver price on the Five Metals Exchange rose by 3 points, which was truly an unprecedented change. American cotton rose by 41 points, and the gold market immediately fell, because the United States had reinstated the gold ban. The opening price was 1,000 yuan, but there were few transactions. Shunlifuchang both accepted orders and once raised the price to over 1,010 yuan. Bingxing Yiyu sold, leading to a decline. Hengyu Dadecheng Laijin hovered around 10 yuan. When Ruixing Hongli Qingfa Yonggan Changxiang all sold, the opening price was 1,004 yuan. The exchange market also opened firm, but initially, there was still some struggle, so it once rebounded from 990 yuan to 1,005 yuan. Afterwards, it immediately trended downward. Foreign telegrams stated that U.S. President Roosevelt declared a ban on gold exports as a way to raise prices and that monetary expansion and the use of silver to pay war debts would be implemented. This triggered a plunge. The after-market opened relatively flat, but later, the exchange market loosened remarkably. Bombay rose by 1 rupee and 6 annas. Foreign telegrams also reported that the United States was planning to purchase a large number of silver ounces, and people's confidence weakened further. For a time, selling pressure was very strong, and prices fell rapidly, once dropping to 966 yuan (breaking the 700 tael mark, equivalent to 690.69 silver). Then it leveled off slightly, and the closing price was 971.5 yuan. It was observed that the environment was unfavorable throughout the day, and sellers outnumbered buyers, marking an unprecedented plunge since the abolition of taels and the introduction of the yuan. The future is indeed more ominous than auspicious. Early red count was at an additional 28 yuan, four-five point swap rate short sellers offered 7.5 yuan, May-June 14 yuan, April-June 20 yuan 5 jiao. The market situation for the day is recorded below.

The morning opened at 1,004 yuan, a sharp drop of 52.2 jiao compared to the previous close. Goods opened at 2 yuan, and the exchange market opened with British exchange at 1 shilling and 2.5 pence, a firming of 125 compared to the previous close. American dollars opened at 23.125 yuan, a firming of 1 yuan compared to the previous close. Gan Changxiang and Bingxing both sold, resulting in a price of 1 yuan. Yuanmao Yongchun Yuan Yong then bought, raising the price to 2 yuan. Afterwards, there was a persistent slump, and selling pressure spread. Hengxing Daxing Yongzheng sold, breaking the 1,000 yuan mark. The exchange market also loosened remarkably. Hengxing continued to sell without stopping, and Yongfeng Gan Changxiang also sold, falling by more than ten yuan to 990 yuan. Tongyi Yuanheng took advantage of the low prices to purchase, and the price rose by 5 yuan. Fuchang Fuyu also bought, pushing the price to over 1,000 yuan. Maijia Li bought American dollars for August at 23 yuan, and Yuansheng Yong Zhaofeng Chang came to buy enthusiastically, pushing the price to 0.05 yuan. Hengxing continued to sell, to 1 yuan smooth. Goods were then sold, pulling up to 4.5 yuan. American dollars for August can be settled at 3 yuan. Hengyu then sold to 1 yuan. HSBC bought American dollars for July at 75, still rising to over 3 yuan. The sellers were excited, and Yifeng Yong took the lead, seeing a downward trend. Citibank sold 75 for July, Fuchang Zhifeng Yong sold, falling to within 1,000 yuan. Ruixing came to sell off sharply, and the price fell to 93 yuan. Overseas Silk Prices Soar

丨Up 13% From the Previous Day丨

Yesterday, raw silk prices on the New York Stock Exchange surged along with other commodities, opening at a high of $1.45 this month, up 13% from the 18th. Yokohama spot prices opened at 815 yuan yesterday, also up 8%. In the local market, due to the 6% drop in the US dollar, exporters who sent silk telegrams the day before had to buy back at a loss when the telegrams were converted yesterday. If the upward trend in the US stabilizes, Chinese silk will likely rise. However, the increase in US prices is solely due to the US government's reaffirmation of the ban on gold exports and the possibility of currency inflation. It is questionable whether lowering the US dollar price is beneficial for the US, which has a trade surplus. If the American people push up prices too aggressively, the eventual backlash may be severe. Therefore, continued price increases in silk in the near term are expected, but whether it will last is uncertain.

Discussions

Talking About Good Goods

— Wu

Mentioning the words "good goods" seems a bit unseemly, because "good goods" inevitably implies being driven by greed. Therefore, righteous gentlemen never lightly utter them, even though in their hearts, there is an indescribable joy. If righteous gentlemen feel this way, then those who dare not call themselves righteous gentlemen need not be mentioned. That's why murder and robbery are rampant, stemming from this very principle.

In reality, in today's orderly society, there's no need to shy away from the matter of "good goods." Promotion and wealth are pursued for "good goods," seizing cities and plundering lands are for "good goods," applying thick layers of snow cream on one's face while flirting with the concubines of powerful officials is also for "good goods." Even those who loudly advocate "national goods to save the country" while tapping on their abacuses are primarily after "good goods."

Clearly, anyone who doesn't pursue "good goods" cannot survive in realistic society, because the Gentleman's Kingdom in "Flowers in the Mirror" is merely a writer's fantasy. Moreover, "morality" and "courtesy" are no longer intoxicating opium.

Therefore, the pursuit of "good goods" is now being refined and perfected. The only missing piece is that everyone is still unwilling to express it directly and frankly.

Take recent events, for example. Before the departure of the Central officials for their overseas trip, Committee Member Zhang "abused his power to sell" the naval hospital and conveniently took away the ancient calligraphy and paintings from the Summer Palace. This is perfectly clear: it's for "good goods." The sale of the naval hospital undoubtedly brought in considerable revenue, and the antique calligraphy and paintings naturally fetch a high price. However, Committee Member Zhang is still young after all, and his actions are not very reliable. For instance, the "selling" issue only revolved around "abusing his power." If he could have agreed on the division of spoils beforehand without "abusing his power," then this secret wouldn't have reached the ears of us ordinary folks. Secondly, taking a few items as souvenirs is customary in Chinese officialdom. However, he did so while people were emphasizing saving the country with antiques and turning the Shanghai concessions into a safe deposit box, and he refused to consult with the custodians. Naturally, people would demand their detention. Of course, this is just a round of finger-pointing and barking at the loser, while in reality, they remain extremely polite and respectful to our Committee Member Zhang. After all, they are all from the same family, so it's easy to talk. But this has somewhat increased the evidence that he's overly fond of "good goods."

Secondly, there are also those who only care about "good goods" regardless of everything else. The most obvious example is General Tang Yulin, who is once again a military governor. Cultivating poppies and hiring Japanese technicians to establish a morphine factory are, of course, for "good goods." Later, because "resolving to resist Japan" would ensure ample support, and two million in war bonds could be obtained with just one "expression" of intent, he immediately "resolved to resist Japan" without hesitation. Subsequently, when Chengde was in danger and the Japanese made their move, he had no choice but to pack his valuables and flee overnight to protect his own life and property. Furthermore, after careful inquiries, the income of the "national heroes" was not bad after all, so he has now decided to "prepare for a counterattack," seeking merit to redeem his crimes and asking the central government for titles. Of course, the central officials are all generous and magnanimous, so they'll grant him the title of military governor and give him another opportunity to make money. In this light, General Yang Yulin is merely a military man who has done little to cultivate himself, and his pursuit of "good goods" is too blatant.

However, all things considered, the continuation of such national crises is indeed a good year for those who love "good goods." Although many people reluctantly bought an "aviation save the country" badge, many lords and masters have seized this opportunity to fulfill their desires for "good goods." Alas, this is what is called "national crisis."

Literature and Art

Song of the Public Servant

— Zhu Maoti

Democracy emphasizes equality, servitude has long been banned, so why do officials call themselves servants? They call themselves servants.

Servant is said to be public, civilized people have no patience. I am a master, want to study why.

“How to admire the servant of the Huo family, teasing as a furnace prostitute; or seeking a partner, hoping to match Kang Cheng’s maid.

Willing to be called lowly, not know why. The world heard me, chuckle not stop.

"This dull head, thinking is very corrupt! The political system has been reformed, is today servant the same as the past?

A little bit of love for silk, offensive to small joy. Seeking its greatest desire; it is here not there.

Power enough to abuse subordinates; the power to hold the Emperor. Bribery is public, the door as a market!

Those who chase and drill, licking pus and hemorrhoids; called to make servants, actually made servants.”

I then surprise, overthrow to this extent? "Alas hundreds of millions, it is the heart first die!

Spring

— Shoupu

Spring is here, bringing joy to the world. Faint sunshine, soft wind, filled with warm love. All sentient beings - people, birds, flowers, are frolicking in this intoxicating spring breeze. Everyone feels that the seasons have changed.

But the joy has been taken away, leaving me only desolation and loneliness.

In a short life, everyone has counted more than twenty springs, but none have left a lovely memory. The days have all passed as if in a dream. Spring has been wasted on me.

Early years, in the mother's embrace, should be happy? But at that time, because the mother was sick, it is said that I ate very little milk. I am afraid that crying was inevitable. But wailing is better than sobbing. I finally grew up happily under the protection of my parents, and to this day I can't find even a trace of sadness left over from that time. What about later? I followed the days in a daze, all the way to the present. In the past many days. If you squeeze it out, you may still find some faint shadows, but they are too faint, and a closer look reveals a blur.

I remember it was that spring, Yi wrote a letter saying that we could meet in S after the Lantern Festival. At that time, I really wanted to arrange a good spring, but it was shattered by his illness and ninety days of spring. By the time he recovered, the longed-for cherry blossoms had withered. We faced each other in vain, and never thought about it again. Let the flowers bloom and wither, without leaving any traces. The change of seasons did not cause me any feelings, but I felt colder when the winter wind blew. Now, I have been drifting north and south for four or five years. The old love is like yesterday, but the time is no longer the same. Let the dreamlike life pass by like a dream. Recalling it is futile.

Now, spring has come to the world again, and the spring breeze rekindles people's enthusiasm. All sentient beings are rejoicing, and green lightly floats on the treetops. But in the city, except for the spring breeze that blows everywhere, there is no other feature to be found. Coal cinder and asphalt roads will never grow a blade of grass. The trees standing on the side of the road also have the sickness of the city, not as majestic as those seen in the countryside. Alas, urban life is as gray as asphalt roads. At this time, I remotely imagine the fields of my beautiful hometown of western Zhejiang, which should already be covered with green. Taking advantage of this splendid spring, I bless Yi to understand a lot. The days are easy to disappear.

China's Three Paths Forward

— Bai Tao

Mr. Zhang Boling, President of Nankai University and Chairman of the Tianjin Local Association, recently made his remarks to reporters. He said to reporters: "We have only three paths to take in this serious situation: first, direct negotiations; second, recovering lost territories; and third, resisting to the death. However, given the current dire international situation, even if the government wants to compromise and negotiate, the people will resolutely oppose it. As for recovering lost territories, we are not sufficiently prepared militarily or economically, so there is no way to talk about it. It is undeniable, therefore, that the only broad road is to fight to the death.”

Mr. Zhang is, after all, an older person. He once said to his students: "I founded Nankai University, so I can do whatever I want. What can you do?" But now that the little Japanese have seized the three northeastern provinces, Rehe, and the passes along the Great Wall, the people of the whole country are planning to recover the lost territories to the death. Our Mr. Zhang, however, feels that we are not sufficiently prepared militarily or economically, so we can't do anything to the little Japanese and can only hope to make peace with them. It's a pity that the ignorant commoners are not knowledgeable and do not recognize the times, otherwise our clever

Page 16

Mr. Zhang would have already shouted out the slogan of "direct negotiations"! Now, because of the resolute opposition of the commoners, he has had to abandon this path and take the third path.

"Long-term resistance" and "resistance to the death" are shouted not only by military men, but also by men of letters. The reason is that this path of "resistance to the death" is in line with the Doctrine of the Mean. Since we can't do anything to the little Japanese, and we don't dare to negotiate directly with Japan because of the resolute opposition of the commoners, we are caught in a dilemma between fearing Japan externally and fearing the people internally. In this difficult situation, we can only choose the Doctrine of the Mean and deal with it! Therefore, "resistance to the death," "long-term resistance," and "negotiating while resisting" are the only broad paths!

Let's give the three northeastern provinces and Rehe to the Japanese for the time being, and resist when the little Japanese reach the Great Wall passes. In the event that the little Japanese break through the Great Wall, it would be best to abandon Beiping and Tianjin first, because the terrain of Beiping and Tianjin is flat and there are no natural defenses,

And everywhere there is the risk of being surrounded by the enemy, so abandoning Beiping and Tianjin is not a defeat, but a strategic decision to retreat to the second line of defense in preparation for resistance!

When the little Japanese break into Beiping and Tianjin, we can retreat to the old lands of Feng and Hao and resist again. If we can't hold Feng and Hao, and the little Japanese continue to press on, we can retreat into the Yumen Pass and defend it in preparation for resistance. In short, we will resist wherever the Japanese attack. This is the true meaning of long-term resistance, and this is a moderate approach that takes everything into account. I cannot help but admire Mr. Zhang's wonderful and brilliant views.

The Art of Advertising

— Yu

Many people have discussed the art of navigating the world, but it's often just a nonsensical jumble. In reality, these notions are merely theories; you must apply a formula to turn them into practice, which is the true art of navigating the world. Otherwise, showing off too much can lead to unexpected dangers. Flattery can backfire, and boasting about your abilities can reveal your shortcomings even before you get drunk. The art lies in mastering (A+B)² = A² + 2AB + B² and then applying the formula to (2+3)² = 2² + 2*3 + 3². Only then can you truly grasp the essence of art. The same applies to advertising!

For example, if your establishment is a silk shop, and you notice a competitor thriving by deceptively promoting their products, you might pound your chest and declare, "I guarantee with my integrity that they sell Japanese goods! Our shop only sells genuine domestic products at affordable prices. Since we opened, we've been honest with everyone, young and old. Patriotic individuals who want to buy domestic products, come to us!" But even if you shout yourself hoarse, you won't see any customers. This is because you know the art of advertising but don't know how to apply its formula. How does one apply the formula of art?

Run a large advertisement on the front page of newspapers, stating that your shop has a mountain of inventory and is disregarding costs for a one-week clearance sale. (After one week, you can run another advertisement, claiming that due to popular demand, you are reluctantly extending the sale for another week, emphasizing that this is a rare opportunity not to be missed.) Offer discounts of 91% and give away free gifts. Additionally, hold a one-hour flash sale every day at 9:30 AM, selling woolen cheongsam fabric for one yuan per piece, limited to 1,000 pieces. Offer worsted wool fabric for two yuan per piece, limited to 500 pieces, and add extra fabric to every purchase. This will guarantee that you have to close the iron gates and your staff will be overwhelmed serving customers. You can clear out all your unsold old stock, and fill your pockets. Why not? However, I must state in advance that the 1,000 pieces of woolen cheongsam fabric and 500 pieces of worsted wool fabric don't necessarily have to be real. Even if you have ten pieces, five pieces, or even none, it's fine. It's just a formula of art. If you don't believe me, here's an example of an advertisement:

Isn't dancing all the rage these days? You're sensual, alluring, captivating souls. Friends who crave eroticism are unsure which establishment to choose. So, an advertisement well-versed in the art formula reads: "Researching artistic beauty dancing, overthrowing prostitution style singing and dancing, sensual beauty secret bathroom."

The bathroom is already mysterious enough, so there's no harm in making it a secret. "Overthrowing prostitution style" is a provocation tactic. Last night after 8 PM, I passed by the Chen Ying Shi Memorial Tower, and the iron gates of the establishment were closed, but the crowd of people outside stretched from the pedestrian walkway to the center of the road, with five tramcars slowly navigating through. Disappointed viewers will likely gather in front of the establishment again at 7 PM tonight.

If you understand this, you'll never go hungry. Advertising colleagues, why not come and openly observe, free of charge?

Shopkeeper Communications

Partnership Dispute

Editor Sir:

In May of last year, I partnered with Mr. Yang to open a XX retail outlet. We agreed on a capital of six hundred yuan, each contributing half. If additional capital was needed later, we would each bear half the burden. Upon starting the business, we each paid two hundred yuan and began decorating, purchasing equipment, and starting operations. Subsequently, in June, we each contributed another one hundred yuan, and Mr. Yang signed a contract with the parent company and paid a deposit of two hundred yuan. However, since the opening, Mr. Yang has not concerned himself with the store's affairs, yet he draws a salary of ten yuan from the store each month. In mid-November, I discovered that the deposit supposedly paid by Mr. Yang had been diverted and not actually paid. As a result, the parent company deducted the commission due to our store to cover the deposit. Consequently, our store's finances were almost impossible to maintain, so I borrowed money to cover it. I have repeatedly tried to recover the funds, but he has consistently delayed. It has been a year now, and there is still no concrete indication of repayment. The partnership agreement has also been delayed and not yet finalized. I now urgently need to settle procedures with Mr. Yang, but I cannot think of a simple solution. Therefore, I respectfully request your advice. Sincerely,

Respectfully, Zang Xuehua

X X X X

Editor's Note: When someone suffers a loss, they should naturally seek ways to negotiate and recover what was lost. "Tolerance and generosity" may be words to live by, but in reality, no one wants to suffer a loss. However, while negotiation is necessary, there is something even more important: to immediately stop the loss from continuing. Because past losses are ultimately limited, but future losses are endless. As for negotiation tactics, the first step is to know yourself and your opponent and assess their abilities. The conditions proposed must be within the opponent's capacity to fulfill; otherwise, the request will be delayed because they are unable to accept it. Based on the above theory, "accepting the loss and settling" is truly the only way to negotiate. Therefore, we believe that Mr. Zang does not need to pursue Mr. Yang at this point, as it seems he may genuinely be unable to repay. You might as well let him withdraw his shares. The dry salary he previously received need not be investigated. He contributed three hundred yuan of capital and diverted two hundred yuan of deposit, so he still has one hundred yuan of capital. You might as well be straightforward and quick and return it to him. From then on, make a clean break, and you will take over the store. The dry salary can also be given out without any politeness. If you are strong enough after this, you might want to do it alone. Otherwise, find a proper person to work with you, and do away with your current neither-dead-nor-alive state!

Market

Publication of Hitler's New Book: "Hitler and the New Germany," recently published by the Liming Bookstore on Fourth Ma Road in this city, is not only novel in its subject matter and rich in content, but also employs a beautiful literary style to systematically narrate the bizarre and tortuous development of Hitler from a bricklayer to a key figure on the modern international political stage, making it quite thought-provoking. It also provides a detailed interpretation of the evolution of the National Socialist Party and its relationship with German politics, and the six illustrations are very valuable. It can be used as a reference for those studying German politics and international issues, and can also be read as a novel. It is truly a rare and excellent work.

Novel

Time in Dreams (Serial 33)

— Qin Shouou

(14) Father and Cold Shoulders

This evening, Wu Yi broke his routine and returned home after 7 PM. His wife, Mrs. Liu, and his two sons, Wu Yuan and Wu Meng, were already gathered in the dining room waiting for him.

"Dad! Where did you take Wang Guodong?" Wu Yuan's temperament was even more impatient than his father's. Wu Yi hadn't even sat down yet, and he was already impatiently demanding an answer. The tone of his voice was almost as stern as a police officer interrogating a petty thief about stolen goods. Mrs. Liu also found it very unnatural and thought Wu Yi would inevitably get angry. She quickly looked up at him with a conciliatory smile. Unexpectedly, he showed no reaction as if he hadn't heard anything. What was especially strange was that his thin, dark face was unexpectedly flushed with drink, unlike usual. This made Mrs. Liu uncontrollably panicked!

Indeed, Wu Yi had not been drinking today. He had set aside his drinking time to handle an urgent matter. At this moment, he felt satisfied and happy in his heart, but also paradoxically felt an indescribable emptiness, as if he had lost something priceless, leaving him confused and dazed.

"You're an hour later than usual." Mrs. Liu noticed his mental state from his sluggish movements and didn't dare abandon her responsibility as a wife. She gently walked over, helped him sit in a large wicker chair, and soothed him tenderly.

Wu Yi seemed as exhausted as if he had just returned from a long journey. Although he had entrusted his entire weight to the large wicker chair beneath him, he was still panting deeply. His original vigor seemed to have slipped away because he hadn't been drinking today.

The younger son quickly poured him a cup of tea, and the elder son had no choice but to tolerate his father's silence for the time being, not daring to ask any further questions.

"Suzhen, the things happening at school, I think Yuan'er has already told you!" After resting for more than ten minutes, Wu Yi finally broke the silence and said solemnly to his wife, "Do you know who Wang Guodong is?"

"I don't know!" Mrs. Liu replied sincerely. Because Wu Yi had never told her about Xiao Lin entering X University, and he had never even mentioned that Wang Guodong was Xiao Lin, she naturally couldn't have guessed.

"He is Xiao Lin, Jufeng's child." Wu Yi explained the key point like the finishing touch on a painting. Although his two sons didn't understand the twists and turns, Mrs. Liu immediately understood when she heard this. She immediately knew why Wu Yi had been trying so hard to protect Wang Guodong today. But although she understood, she didn't feel unhappy or express dissatisfaction. Perhaps it was because she wasn't originally from Zhenjiang, so she had always been afraid of jealousy. When Wu Yi was constantly mixing with Jufeng in the past, she had never said a word of complaint. Now that Jufeng was dead and Wu Yi was just taking care of her child, there was naturally even less need to be jealous.
