Film Special

Joan Crawford, as Described by Norma Shearer

— Bing

Norma Shearer and Joan Crawford are both contract actors at MGM. Because they hold similar positions, some say they are intensely competitive behind the scenes. The main reason is that although Norma and Joan work for the same company, they rarely talk or hang out together. Outsiders suspect they harbor secret resentment due to their estrangement, but Norma has now stated that she and Joan have no desire to compete for status whatsoever. Norma is a person of impeccable conduct and an open mind, so what she says is certainly not a false pretense.

Norma said, "Although Joan Crawford and I are both at MGM, my time is very limited. Everything at home has to be settled first, and only the remaining time is for my work. Joan and I are different. She is diligent in her work, and her household affairs are managed by others. Moreover, she has no children and can focus on the set. So, my working hours are often at home, while Joan works all day on the set and has very little free time. Therefore, we rarely have a day to chat freely, but our relationship is absolutely fine. It's just that we spend little time together, so it's no wonder outsiders suspect we are competing for fame and fortune."

"Joan Crawford is the friend I consider the most perfect. Her amiability and loyalty are praised by everyone in Hollywood. She has never had a problem with anyone. Although I don't see or talk to her every day, I know her personality completely. And I don't know how to be jealous or resentful of others. Moreover, I don't have that much energy to spend on scheming. Who's more artistically accomplished, Joan or me, that has to be evaluated fairly by the public and by the camera. Does competing necessarily make someone better? I don't think Joan has that intention at all, and I know I'm not capable of that kind of scheming. I consider Joan and I to be good friends, and Joan wouldn't dislike me and abandon me."

"In terms of superficial fame, although I have been hailed as the Queen of MGM, it's just an empty title. I really work too little. Since 'Smilin' Through' was completed last year, I've only filmed one movie, 'Smiling Through.' I still try my best to conserve time and squeeze out time by having Charles manage many household affairs. As for Joan's works, after 'Grand Hotel,' there were 'Rain,' 'Today We Live,' and the recent 'Turnabout.' Although 'Rain' was filmed by Fox, borrowing Joan, it is also a glory for MGM. So, I recognize that I am not as good as Joan. I know that she is more diligent than me. I respect her, and I am not jealous of her. I especially respect her treatment of people, and she doesn't act like a red star or treat people with arrogance."

Film Review

Review of "State Fair"

— Wanshi

Obviously, the overall economic panic does not exclude the film industry. Therefore, American film producers have to rely on "stars" to make extreme appeals. Although they are all originally able to stand on their own and individually become the protagonists of various films, under the current wave of economic collapse, they have to lower themselves a little and act in a film with many "stars."

First, there was MGM's "Grand Hotel," and now there is Fox's "State Fair."

Because there are so many "stars" in this film, and it is inconvenient to demote anyone to a supporting role, the screenwriter has to create a script that can accommodate many protagonists in order to suit this special condition. Regarding this point, I think some people might say, "This film has no protagonist." If that is the case, then I believe he has definitely ignored the main reason why Fox wanted to film this film.

As mentioned above, since there are so many protagonists in this film, then director Henry King must pay attention to each star separately, and it is best to be very balanced. Therefore, in order to be thorough, the director must take all three aspects into consideration in the depiction of the State Fair, and at the same time, editing will inevitably be a little troublesome. Because this play is performed in the form of comedy, it does not need to be too serious in tone, so the director must make the whole play very lively, and even insert extremely natural jokes at any time. However, his depiction of the love between the two pairs of men and women does not seem very lively. The main thing is that the same scenes are too many, such as the reporter and Margie hugging in the car, but it is repeated more than three times. However, the love talks on the hill are different in content each time, so they are of course more tasteful. Others, such as Margie being overjoyed and losing herself on the reporter's shoulder, and Wayne and Emily's warm night, only the voices are heard, but no people are seen. The picture uses the spring breeze blowing the curtains to enhance the tender mood. It is indeed very beautiful and vivid.

Regarding performance, I don't want to say too much. Anyway, each star has his inherent achievements. The lighting is most worthy of attention. They are all so quiet and soft.

As for the meaning of this film, then the consistent satire throughout is not to be ignored. The elderly couple's desire for fame and wealth, the merchants' exaggerated shouts, the judges' ugly states, Wayne's reluctantly taking up with an old flame after a broken heart, and the most severe is actually using the lust of a pig to illustrate the passion of young men and women.

A lightly sketched work like this can actually achieve such great success, of course we have to admit that this is a relatively special harvest in American films. But we also fully understand the producer's hard work.

Review of "Her Heart"

— Ailian

"Her Heart" is such a poetic name! But for this film, this title is too broad and impractical. Judging from the position, capital, and other aspects of Yueming Company, this film is not only much better than "The Great Hero of Guandong" and "Female Escort," but even the recently released "The Real Man" is not as good as this one. This shows that it is at a stage of gradual progress.

In the productions of small companies, the story is always very long. Indeed, a long story can save the director a lot of effort. The plot is like this:

A vain girl, her father is a school director. In a certain year, a talented and handsome young man graduated, and they fell in love. However, a secretary of the school director also has a crush on the girl, so a love triangle is formed. The secretary also uses the merits of the beauty contest to threaten the girl, and uses hooligans to forcibly kidnap the girl. At that time, the young man and the girl's cousin also used the police to capture them. The result is of course that the talented man and the beautiful woman become a couple.

This plot, although lacking in satire, is generally passable. The organization can also be graded.

The director is Ren Pengnian, the boss of Yueming. He is very unfamiliar with this kind of social drama, so mistakes are inevitable, the insertion is not good, and the editing cannot be called art.

The most important actor is the new star who plays that girl? Huo Feilun, she is very beautiful. This is her first time on camera. Although there are many overly pretentious places, the director should be responsible for this. She feels her personal talent is not bad, and the young man Luo Kebeng has made some progress in this film compared to "The Real Man," but the surface is still much worse. Only fighting is his forte. It is not necessary to talk about the other important roles, as they seem too civilized.

The photography is ordinary. The light is still sunlight. Although the subtitles repeatedly prompt that it is late at night, it does not look like a night scene at all. Some of the scenery is not bad, but some are so fake that it is obvious at a glance. There are not many subtitles, but the wording lacks research. The music provided by the Central Grand Theater is also extremely boring.

There are many inappropriate places in this drama, especially the costumes. For example, the rich man's nephew is dressed like a hooligan, while the hooligans are dressed in suits and leather shoes, with a graceful demeanor. There are more loopholes. For example, the big fight at the end is simply acting. When a bullet hits the face, in addition to a little black stain, there is no blood at all. The humorous insertions not only do not make people laugh, but also mistake the plot. In short, these are all counterproductive.

In the second half, it can be very tense, but the exterior scenes, such as running, etc.

Page 20

, are filmed too much, which makes it feel lax.

In the end, I think this kind of happy ending is indeed welcomed by low-level tastes, and all the technology is only thought to be satisfactory by people with low-level ideas. Therefore, I hope that Yueming Company will continue to work hard to move forward.

Warner Pyle and the White Elephant

Hua·Ming·

When Warner Pyle was sixteen years old, he followed his father to work with the workers. His father was a laborer, and Warner found a job herding elephants. At that time, Warner only wanted to be an elephant herder for the rest of his life. He probably never dreamed of Hollywood!

Among the animals, the skin of the white elephant is the thickest. Other animals know pain even when whipped a few times, but it is not easy to tame a white elephant even if the whip is destroyed. Because of this, a person who herds white elephants absolutely cannot be competent without patience. When Warner first arrived at the ranch, the owner did not know his character and asked him to manage the white elephants. Warner grew up with the workers, so he naturally had some rough habits. The first few days were extremely difficult. Unexpectedly, Warner Pyle actually worked as an elephant herder for more than twenty years, training himself into a character who was able to endure and was cunning, resourceful, and sometimes very sincere. All of these are the basis for his ability to stand out in the film industry today and the strange style that no one can confront.

The big key to Warner's future was of course "Grand Hotel," but the reason why he was able to be on par with the top-notch stars of Hollywood, Greta Garbo, the Barrymore brothers, and Joan Crawford, all four big stars, was actually due to the success of "The Champ." Warner and Jackie Cooper were awarded by the American Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences in 1932 for "The Champ." At the same time, this film was the source of Warner Pyle's good fortune.

In "Grand Hotel," we got a deeper impression of Warner. His exploitation of the capitalist's sinister methods is exactly the transformation of his methods of dealing with white elephants. His cunning attitude is perfectly portrayed, as the newspapers have already concluded.

Movies Showing in Taverns

Ying·Dai·

Movie Fans Can Eat Roast Pork

Ever since the area of Jugoslav Nicodin began transporting roast pork to the Belgrade area, general movie fans began to have a special craving for fragrant roast pork.

But general movie fans, after eating roast pork, stopped going to movies in order to save money. As a result, movie theaters were empty, and those owners began to think of special ways to attract moviegoers.

One owner published a huge advertisement, saying that those who went to the movie theater to watch a movie would be given a free slice of roast pork without paying a penny.

However, at the same time, a tavern invented a countermeasure. He built a room in the tavern to show movies. Those who went to his tavern to eat roast pork could watch movies for free. As a result, the movie theater's business was completely stolen.

It is said that in that tavern, movies are shown in a dark room during the day, and in the garden at night if the weather is clear. This method is of course very novel. Since its implementation, business has been very good, and the sales of roast pork are especially amazing!

Prelude to "Spring Tide"

Zhou·Jing·Zhi·

After the news that "Spring Tide" will soon be released in Shanghai spread, my heart was filled with joy. "Spring Tide" is an immortal masterpiece by the great Russian writer Turgenev. Although it has now been adapted into a Chinese script, its core remains, and it is still so profound and moving. In addition, director Zheng Yingshi poured his heart and soul into it, making it a special force in domestic sound films.

The plot is: "A weak-willed young man abandons his lover due to erotic temptation, and then awakens to his past mistakes after suffering greatly. However, what methods can be used to compensate for the condemnation of conscience? A single slip can cause eternal regret!"

What is even more worthy of introduction is that the clarity of the sound on the film is the best recording ever, which was recorded by Yan Heming. I have unlimited hope for his future.

Movie News Snippets

Song · Ling ·

The film industry has initiated a joint film production to raise funds for a "Movie Plane." The preparatory committee met the other day at the YMCA in Ba Xian Qiao and resolved that the script for the film should take the promotion of aviation to save the nation as its general theme, further divided into sub-items to showcase the reactions and efforts of all sectors regarding saving the nation through aviation. The sub-items are tentatively set as twelve categories: agriculture, industry, commerce, education, the performing arts, beggars, artists, children, the military, government, doctors, and lawyers. Each film company will be responsible for one or two items, and the filming will be divided among them. During screening, they will still be connected as a single, complete film.

Those in China who have researched sound films include Shi Shipan's "Aisitone," Yan Hemen's "Hemingtone," Zhu Qingxian's "Qingxian Style," and a certain university professor's "Shiduotong." Among them, those who have already filmed movies include Qingxian Style's "Spring Breeze Willow Branches" and Hemingtone's "Spring Tide." It is now heard that Zhu Qingxian's "Bringing Glory to the Nation," produced on behalf of Jinan Company, has also been completed, and its results are said to be an improvement over "Spring Breeze Willow Branches."

"Pursuit," directed by Qiu Qixiang and starring Li Minghui, recently opened at the Beijing Theater and is reportedly sold out every day. When the film premiered at Xinguang, the song "When Will We Meet Again," sung by Li Minghui in the first scene during a farewell gathering at a certain university, was later deemed too lengthy and the melody not very good, so it was re-filmed and replaced. The first scene now being shown in Beijing features Li Minghui singing "Winter Clothing Song."

Westerners' Views on Films that Insult China

Xin ·

The bad trend of Western films insulting Chinese people has become increasingly intense in recent years. All such films brought to China have been repeatedly banned from screening. It is evident how much this is criticized by the people of our country. However, various film companies still refuse to rein themselves in, and continue to produce such films, gradually damaging the feelings between the Chinese and American people, which worries knowledgeable people. The American film magazine published an article on March 18, representing the views of Jiao Lin Yanaide, the American Commercial Counselor stationed in Shanghai, on films that insult China. His words were righteous and direct, no less than a wake-up call to the entire American film industry. A translation of his words is specially recorded below:

"If American film companies could conduct accurate and reasonable investigations into Chinese customs, national conditions, and social organization when filming and performing movies about Chinese people, then the relationship between China and the United States and the interests of the United States in China would be further strengthened.

"Recently, film companies have repeatedly received reports that films depicting Chinese people have suffered enormous criticism and setbacks overseas. This is because the portrayals of Chinese people in these films are full of absurdities. They either call Chinese people 'Chinaman' or depict Chinese people with pigtails, and even the dialogue uses the unbearable 'Pidgin English.' Furthermore, the depictions of Chinese people's fondness for gambling and opium addiction, including the bizarre shapes of low-class squalid gambling dens and opium dens, as well as depictions of kidnappers and robbers, are all untrue. Today's China is no longer what it used to be. Opium smokers have disappeared, 'Pidgin English' is only spoken by the lower classes, and pigtails have long been abolished."

Movie Novel - A Record of Loyal Souls

Cavalcade (3) Ne ·

Qi Yin drank with him, her heart a blur, not knowing whether she was happy or sad. But this new century, the first minute of the first day of the new hundred years, Qi Yin would remember it forever: that icy night, the distant chimes, the torchlight procession in the streets, the factory whistles welcoming the new year, the flowers offered by the servants, Robert's smile, the children's faces full of wonder, and everything else. But what she remembered most clearly was the song of Oran Hill sung in the streets. From then on, every time she thought of this memorable night, she would hear the tune of Oran Hill in her ears.

But even after hearing the tune of Oran Hill, the surging in her heart had not stopped, and an exhilarating marching song began to play again. Although Robert was among the crowd, singing "Girls, he is the Queen's Warrior," Qi Yin stood at the door listening, her heart breaking inch by inch. And also, at that moment on the pier, Qi Yin, in her grief and numbness, could still feel Ellen standing next to her, holding that child, that blessed, carefree child, who did not understand that many of these soldiers going to South Africa would be buried in foreign lands, never to return.

The gong sounded, and the ship was about to set sail. Robert said to Qi Yin, "I want to kiss you, then you turn your head and, as usual, talk to me while walking forward. You don't have to look back."

"Yes," Qi Yin's voice choked in her throat. She talked to Robert: "I'm glad I didn't bring the children. They're too young. How would they know all this? Isn't Qiao Yi a little under the weather? It's better not to bring him out." Although Qi Yin's mouth was saying irrelevant small talk, in her heart she was crying and shouting, begging him not to go. She continued the conversation: "You're not here now. I know. I feel like you've already left, Robert: : : Robert: : :"

She hurriedly turned her head, and the ship was slowly moving. She looked for Robert in a large crowd, but her eyes were full of tears, and she couldn't see anything even a foot away. How could she find him? She felt Ellen supporting her. Ellen's own man had also gone to war. The two of them, sharing the same fate, supported each other and returned to that strangely empty and quiet home.

From then on, the days were entirely managed by Ellen alone. She also had a man fighting in South Africa, so she could understand Qi Yin's pain. Sometimes she would tell the children to be quiet so that Qi Yin could get some sleep, or she would tease the children and play noisily to cheer Qi Yin up. These were all Ellen's efforts to protect Qi Yin. The clever and kind Ellen was no longer just an ordinary servant woman, but a good companion in loneliness.
